That simplifies to f(-y + y) = f(0) = 1. So the left side becomes 1. Therefore, 1 = y² + f(-y)f(y) for all y.So we have y² + f(-y)f(y) = 1 for all y. Rearranging, f(-y)f(y) = 1 - y². We will consider these two cases separately.First, assume that f(1)=0. Substitute x=t and y=1-t, and then x=1-t and y=t, which gives the two equationsbegin{aligned}f(t) & =(1-t)^{2}+f(t) f(1-t) f(1-t) & =t^{2}+f(t) f(1-t)end{aligned}Subtracting these equations gives f(t)-f(1-t)=(1-t)^{2}-t^{2}=1-2 t, so f(1-t)=f(t)+2 t-1. Substituting this into the first of the above two equations givesf(t)=(1-t)^{2}+f(t)^{2}+(2 t-1) f(t)which can be rewritten asf(t)^{2}+(2 t-2) f(t)+(1-t)^{2}=0or (f(t)-(1-t))^{2}=0. We need to solve the inequality ( (x + 2014)^2 f(x + 2014) - 4f(-2) > 0 ).First, we note that ( x + 2014 ) must be in the domain ( (-infty, 0) ), implying ( x < -2014 ). This narrows down the solution set to a subset of ( (-infty, -2014) ).Next, we consider the given differential inequality ( 2f(x) + x f'(x) > x^2 ). This leads us to consider the function ( g(x) = x^2 f(x) ), whose derivative ( g'(x) = x(2f(x) + x f'(x)) ) is less than ( x^3 ).We integrate this inequality from ( -2 ) to ( y ) (where ( y < -2 )) and find that ( g(y) - 4f(-2) > frac{y^4 - 16}{4} ). For ( y leq -2 ), this implies ( y^4 geq 16 ), leading to ( y leq -2 ).Substituting back ( y = x + 2014 ), we get ( x + 2014 leq -2 ), which simplifies to ( x leq -2016 ). Therefore, the solution set is ( (-infty, -2016) ).Thus, the correct answer is (boxed{C}).]

🔑:AnalysisThis problem examines the use of monotonicity to solve inequalities. Constructing a function from the given conditions and utilizing the relationship between function monotonicity and derivatives is key to solving this problem. Transforming the inequality allows us to reach a conclusion.SolutionGiven 2f(x)+xf′(x) > x^{2}, (x 0,Since F(x) is a decreasing function on (-infty,0),From F(x+2014) > F(-2),We get x+2014 < -2,Which means x < -2016.Therefore, the correct choice is boxed{text{C}}.

Tangent line at (P(x_1, y_1)) on (y = ln x): - The derivative of (ln x) is (frac{1}{x}), so the slope at (x_1) is (frac{1}{x_1}). - The equation of the tangent line is (y = frac{1}{x_1}(x - x_1) + ln x_1), which simplifies to (y = frac{1}{x_1}x + (ln x_1 - 1)).2. Tangent line at (Q(x_2, y_2)) on (y = e^x): - The derivative of (e^x) is (e^x), so the slope at (x_2) is (e^{x_2}). - The equation of the tangent line is (y = e^{x_2}(x - x_2) + e^{x_2}), which simplifies to (y = e^{x_2}x + e^{x_2}(1 - x_2)).Since these tangent lines are the same, their slopes and y-intercepts must be equal:- Equating the slopes: (frac{1}{x_1} = e^{x_2}).- Equating the y-intercepts: (ln x_1 - 1 = e^{x_2}(1 - x_2)).From the slope equation, we get (e^{x_2} = frac{1}{x_1}), which implies (x_2 = -ln x_1).Substituting (e^{x_2} = frac{1}{x_1}) into the y-intercept equation:[ln x_1 - 1 = frac{1}{x_1}(1 - x_2)]Multiplying both sides by (x_1):[x_1 ln x_1 - x_1 = 1 - x_2]Rearranging gives:[x_2 = 1 + x_1 - x_1 ln x_1]We also know (x_2 = -ln x_1). Equating the two expressions for (x_2):[-ln x_1 = 1 + x_1 - x_1 ln x_1]Rearranging terms:[x_1 ln x_1 - ln x_1 - x_1 - 1 = 0]Factoring out (ln x_1):[ln x_1 (x_1 - 1) - (x_1 + 1) = 0]This simplifies to:[ln x_1 = frac{x_1 + 1}{x_1 - 1}]To find (frac{2}{x_1 - 1} + x_2), we use (x_2 = -ln x_1) and the equation (ln x_1 = frac{x_1 + 1}{x_1 - 1}):[frac{2}{x_1 - 1} + x_2 = frac{2}{x_1 - 1} - ln x_1]Substituting (ln x_1 = frac{x_1 + 1}{x_1 - 1}):[frac{2}{x_1 - 1} - frac{x_1 + 1}{x_1 - 1} = frac{2 - (x_1 + 1)}{x_1 - 1} = frac{1 - x_1}{x_1 - 1} = -1]Thus, the final answer is (boxed{-1}).]

🔑:To solve the problem, we first need to find the equations of the tangent lines to the curves at the given points and then equate them to find the relationship between x_1 and x_2.1. Finding the tangent line to y=ln x at P(x_{1}, y_{1}):The derivative of y=ln x is y'=frac{1}{x}. Thus, the equation of the tangent line at point P(x_{1}, y_{1}) is given by:[y-y_{1}=frac{1}{x_{1}}(x-x_{1})]Since y_{1}=ln x_{1}, we can rewrite this as:[y-ln x_{1}=frac{1}{x_{1}}(x-x_{1})]2. Finding the tangent line to y=e^{x} at Q(x_{2}, y_{2}):The derivative of y=e^{x} is y'=e^{x}. Thus, the equation of the tangent line at point Q(x_{2}, y_{2}) is given by:[y-y_{2}=e^{x_{2}}(x-x_{2})]Since y_{2}=e^{x_{2}}, we can rewrite this as:[y-e^{x_{2}}=e^{x_{2}}(x-x_{2})]3. Equating the slopes of the tangent lines:Since the tangent lines are the same, their slopes must be equal. Therefore, we have:[frac{1}{x_{1}}=e^{x_{2}}]And their y-intercepts must also be equal, leading to:[ln x_{1}-1=e^{x_{2}}(1-x_{2})]4. Finding the relationship between x_1 and x_2:From frac{1}{x_{1}}=e^{x_{2}}, we can deduce that x_{2}=-ln x_{1}. Substituting this into the equation for the y-intercepts gives:[ln x_{1}-1=frac{1}{x_{1}}(1+ln x_{1})]Simplifying this equation, we find:[ln x_{1}-1=frac{2}{{x}_{1}-1}]5. Calculating frac{2}{{x_1}-1}+x_{2}:Given x_{2}=-ln x_{1}, we substitute this into the equation to find:[frac{2}{{x_1}-1}+x_{2}=ln x_{1}-1-ln x_{1}=-1]Therefore, the final answer is boxed{-1}.

We find the following minimal solutions with (x leq y leq z):1. ((2, 4, 13))2. ((2, 5, 8))3. ((3, 3, 7))Next, we count all permutations of these solutions:- For ((2, 4, 13)) and ((2, 5, 8)), each with 3 distinct elements, there are (3! = 6) permutations each.- For ((3, 3, 7)) with two identical elements, there are (3) permutations.Summing these, we get:[6 + 6 + 3 = 15]Thus, the number of all positive integer solutions is (boxed{15}).,<think>Okay, so I need to find all positive integer solutions (x, y, z) to the equation arctan(1/x) + arctan(1/y) + arctan(1/z) = π/4. Key Observations: - Each term (arctan frac{1}{x}) must be less than (frac{pi}{4}), implying (x, y, z geq 2). - Using the tangent addition formula, we derive that the equation can be transformed into a form involving integer solutions for (x, y, z).2. 🔑:1. Given the equation ([x] cdot {x} = 2005x), we start by expressing (x) in terms of its integer and fractional parts: [ x = [x] + {x} ] where ([x]) is the greatest integer less than or equal to (x) and ({x} = x - [x]) is the fractional part of (x).2. Substitute (x = [x] + {x}) into the given equation: [ [x] cdot {x} = 2005([x] + {x}) ]3. Distribute the 2005 on the right-hand side: [ [x] cdot {x} = 2005[x] + 2005{x} ]4. Rearrange the equation to isolate ({x}): [ [x] cdot {x} - 2005{x} = 2005[x] ] [ {x}([x] - 2005) = 2005[x] ]5. Solve for ({x}): [ {x} = frac{2005[x]}{[x] - 2005} ]6. The condition (0 leq {x} < 1) must hold. We analyze this condition for different ranges of ([x]).7. Case 1: ([x] < 2005) - If ([x] < 2005), then ([x] - 2005 < 0), making the denominator negative. - For ({x}) to be non-negative, the numerator must also be non-positive: [ 2005[x] leq 0 implies [x] leq 0 ] - Let (n = -[x]), where (n geq 0). Then: [ {x} = frac{2005(-n)}{-n - 2005} = frac{-2005n}{-n - 2005} = frac{2005n}{n + 2005} ] - The condition (0 leq {x} < 1) becomes: [ 0 leq frac{2005n}{n + 2005} < 1 ] - Simplify the inequality: [ 2005n < n + 2005 implies 2004n < 2005 implies n < frac{2005}{2004} ] - Since (n) is an integer, the only possible values are (n = 0) or (n = 1): - If (n = 0), then ([x] = 0) and ({x} = 0), so (x = 0). - If (n = 1), then ([x] = -1) and: [ {x} = frac{2005 cdot 1}{1 + 2005} = frac{2005}{2006} ] [ x = [x] + {x} = -1 + frac{2005}{2006} = frac{-1}{2006} ]8. Case 2: ([x] > 2005) - If ([x] > 2005), then ([x] - 2005 > 0), making the denominator positive. - For ({x}) to be less than 1, the numerator must be less than the denominator: [ 2005[x] < [x] - 2005 implies 2004[x] < -2005 implies [x] < frac{-2005}{2004} ] - Since ([x]) is an integer, there are no integers less than (frac{-2005}{2004}) that are greater than 2005. Thus, there are no solutions in this case.9. Therefore, the only solutions are: [ x = 0 quad text{and} quad x = frac{-1}{2006} ]The final answer is (boxed{x = 0 text{ and } x = frac{-1}{2006}}).
